<h2>All Reviews</h2>

<ol>
    <li> This shaves CLOSE!  I also like it that I can see the percentage of charge. Reviews said it was good--smoked prior Norelco (glad it got lost). Quality. Tried to pick up another for one of my sons but the price went up about $39.  I didn&#x27;t realize I got such a good original deal.</li>
    <li> Excellent electric razor.  Very close shave with a swivel head that can follow the curves of your face.  Battery lasts about 2 weeks.</li>
    <li> I much prefer the Panasonics to all the other shavers I&#x27;ve used, including high-end Norelco and Braun. Apparently the skin on my throat is VERY sensitive, since a blade - ANY blade when I try to get very close - leaves me covered with dots of blood to be followed the next day by spots of infection.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;The weak point, for me, with the Panasonics is the little spring-loaded plastic tabs on either side. Eventually they give way. And, though the mechanics of the shaver are fine, if the head won&#x27;t stay on, it&#x27;s not of much use. Would be nice if they were replaceable!&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;The other &#x27;problem&#x27; I&#x27;ve encountered is a leakage of something appearing to be oil under the soft rubbery plastic on the handle. It appears to me the lifespan of one of these shavers, given these two factors, is only a few years.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;But, would I buy this again? Yup. Works very well.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;NO shaver that has claimed to be a &#x27;single pass&#x27; shaver IS - at least not for me. At 66, my beard is much thinner than at 21 - which has its benefits. But even at that, stretching the skin and multiple passes is required! This Panasonic is no exception. But it is GENTLE and of course powerful.</li>
    <li> I agree this is a great electric razor but it isn&#x27;t perfect. It still leaves hairs on me after several passes so I am not sure if I am doing something wrong?  I have tried with shaving cream and pulling my skin but with shaving cream you can&#x27;t see if you got the hair.</li>
    <li> I have a light beard, but I still need to shave every day to try to look somewhat civilized. I used an electric shaver for several years before switching to blades about 10 years ago, which were faster and closer than my old Norelco electric razor. However, I recently developed some sort of allergic reaction to the lubricating bar that now comes on Gillette blades, specifically itching on my neck and chin. So when I saw that Amazon had the Panasonic ES-LA63-S on a \\&quot;Today&#x27;s Deals\\&quot; sale for $99.99, I decided to give it a try. Glad I did!&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;The Panasonic shaves me very quickly, very closely, and very comfortably -- better in all respects than the blades I was using. It&#x27;s light and easy to hold, and the head pivots to follow the contours of my face. It charges quickly -- one hour from zero to a full charge -- and it looks as if a charge will last me a couple of weeks at least. It can be used wet, so there&#x27;s no worry about dropping it in a sink full of water, and it&#x27;s easy to clean using liquid soap and water (it even has a turbo setting specifically for cleaning). Lastly, the digital readout provides a lot of information, including the charge level, how much time you&#x27;ve used it, an alert when it needs cleaning, and a couple of other things. And the built-on trimmer is 1000% better at trimming sideburns than the single blade that&#x27;s on the Gillette cartridges for that purpose. Oh, yeah - it comes with a 2-year warranty. All in all a very good buy!&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;p.s. - If you try to register the razor on Panasonic&#x27;s website, you may run into a problem with the serial number. The site insists that the number contain 9 to 11 digits, but the serial number on the razor is only 7 digits. If you enter just those 7 digits, the system will not accept your registration. I called Panasonic and discovered that the workaround is to add the letters SN before the 7-digit serial number, and the system will then accept your registration.</li>
    <li> Bought this as a second (travel) shaver for the ES-LA93 I have. One thing is that this one doesn&#x27;t have the charging contacts on the back for use with the docking station. Beyond that, works well - as good as the other one.</li>

    <li> This review won&#x27;t convince straight razor nor safety blade users to switch.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I have used this razor for month so I can&lt;br /&gt;For years, both my father and I have used Philips products (the items manufactured in Holland) when there was no such thing as re-chargable razors.&lt;br /&gt;The rotary system is fine, until you purchase the replacement heads.  Then you collapse in a state of shock.&lt;br /&gt;I replaced my old Philips Cool Shave as I was recharging it every 3 days and it was taking 8 hours a day to charge.&lt;br /&gt;I contemplated Braun, but I read some poor reviews on this site and others as well.&lt;br /&gt;This Panasonic model ES-LA63 is sufficient for what I required.  The model above this version (ES-LA93) has the self cleaning function.  That is OK, until you have to purchase the replacement cleaning solution.  It is a slight incremental benefit that you must consistently pay for maintenance.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Other comments talk about the noise that comes from the razor.  It is a non-issue.  Anything mechanical makes a noise.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Wet shaves are impressive.  Face and under the nose is very good in removing hair.&lt;br /&gt;The neck (LIKE ALL ELECTRICS) require time and technique.  Remember, it is just a razor.     <li> GREAT FOR CUTTING A STRAIGHT BEARD - NOT SO GOOD FOR A AREA WHERE HAIR GROWS AT AN ANGLE , I&#x27;LL GIVE IT ANOTHER WEEK</li>
    <li> At the beginning the performance was not that great, but as per other users&#x27; recommendations I decided to stick with the shaver for a little while. My skin is now sort of used to the shaver and you tend to get better results over time.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;As other users have mentioned, getting rid of skin hair around your neck is somewhat difficult so you need to stretch your skin to make it (it doesn&#x27;t work all the time though).&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I like it because it is pretty comfortable for a quick shave, though I always fallback to razors for cleaner shaves.</li>
    <li> When I started shaving there were very few options available:  single razor blades, straight-edge, disposables and a few electric models.  I tried everything.  Back then, the electric razors I tried, pulled on the hairs rather than cutting them so I gave-up on electric razors believing that my beard was just too tough for an electric to handle.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;There&#x27;s no argument that the 2, 3, 4 and 5 blade razors revolutionized shaving starting in the late 1980&#x27;s / early 1990&#x27;s.  Then came the sticker shock of the replacement blades.  But that&#x27;s the dream, right?  Create a product that everyone needs that&#x27;s disposable that they have to buy again and again.  But that&#x27;s an expensive trap for consumers...&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;With that said, when I researched the Panasonic, I was hesitant because of the cost.  Then, after doing the math, I realized that I spent more than that on the yearly cost of replacement blades and so bought the electric.  To be honest, even before the first shave, I was prepared to return the razor.  After my early experiences with electric razors, I didn&#x27;t have high hopes...&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;To my amazement and surprise - it gave me a clean and fun shave.  I actually look forward to shaving every day; I haven&#x27;t felt that way since I was a boy (you know, that time in every young boy&#x27;s life when we were all in a rush to be all grown-up).&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I&#x27;m not going to comare electric to blades because I find that comparison utterly ridiculous - and I think the reviewers here who have done so, just like the sound of their own voice.  The fact is, I&#x27;ll use a blade from time to time but for daily or ever 2x daily maintenance (the touch-up before an evening out at the theatre), I&#x27;ll be using the Panasonic.</li>

    <li> This is a beautiful and high quality shaver.  It comes with a soft, zippered form-fitting case.  I don&#x27;t think its leather, but looks like it will hold up for a long time.  I did have a shaver about 15 years ago that came with a much nicer leather custom case.  For the price of this shaver, I sort of expected one like that.  Oh well.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;This shaves very gently.  I&#x27;ve had ones that could easily cut into your adams apple or around your lips if you pushed too hard in those areas.  This one is very easy to wash with a drop of liquid soap and warm running water.  I find it helpful to rub some clipper oil on the inside of the cutting foil with a Q-tip after washing.  It will make the blades last much longer and provide a smoother shave.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I am 47 years old and have owned maybe 6 or 7 electrics and this is, by far, the most effective.  Battery life is good.  I get about 5 shaves per charge.  I only use it dry, so I can&#x27;t say how it works wet or in the shower, but it says it is safe to do so.  It&#x27;s a lot of money, but a great shaver.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;If you are having trouble with razor bumps, and/or ingrown hairs, this may help with that problem.  This shaver will not cut hair below the skin surface.  Supposedly, even with a razor blade, you are not supposed to cut hair against the grain for this reason.  So, if you compare a shave with a blade NOT against the grain to this shaver, I think this electric does a better job.  This model has a timer on it so it tells you how long it took to shave and I average right about 5 minutes.</li>

There&#x27;s no need to crack it open to clean it.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;- Pop-Up Trimmer&lt;br /&gt;The pop-up trimmer does as good a job as a dedicated trimmer.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;- Good Ergonomics&lt;br /&gt;The shaver is comfortable to hold.     <li> I owned an older Panasonic razor, but eventually the battery died and I just trashed it and went back to wet-shaving.     <li> I&#x27;ve tried many different electric razors over the past 15 years, whether it was from Braun, Norelco, or Remington.  Prior to testing the Panasonic ES-LA63-S I had been using a Braun Cruzer.  After using the ES-LA63-S for 3 weeks, I can definitely say it&#x27;s the closest shave I&#x27;ve ever had with an electric razor.&lt;br /&gt;The Panasonic ES-LA63-S has two motors and two blade sets housed inside a giant shaver head that contains three foils and a hair lifter/comb piece.  The shaver head really is big, which is a strength and a weakness of the unit.  The head of the unit tilts to accommodate the contours of your chin and neck, but you can also lock the head in place so it does not tilt.  In addition, there is a pop up trimmer on the unit for sideburns and such.  The ES-LA63-S has a fairly large blue LED screen on the handle that tells you how much battery power is remaining, how long your shaving session lasted, whether the battery is being charged and if the cleaning mode is on.  The shaver feels solid and heavy in your hand--in a good way.  The construction of it makes it feel like it will have no durability issues.  This Panasonic also comes with an AC adapter and a very basic carrying case.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Cleaning the unit is pretty easy, and is probably has the best electric shaver cleaning system that I&#x27;ve ever seen.  To clean you place several small drops of liquid hand soap across the top of the foils and then hold down the power button in order to enter \\&quot;turbo mode.\\&quot;  The blades vibrate really fast and lather up the foils and blades themselves.  You let that run for 20 seconds, stop and then rinse.  The foil cover comes off easily so you can rinse out the entire head, inside and out.  Works way better than having to use those mini-brushes that inexpensive shavers come with, and it&#x27;s far cheaper than having to buy replacement cleaning cartridges for some other shavers, like several of the Braun series.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;The ES-LA63-S covers a lot of surface area in one motion and cuts hairs really close for an efficient shave.  The timer says most of my shaves last about 3 minutes.  I tried it both wet and dry, and I prefer to use it dry after a shower.  The first week that I used this shaver I noticed an increased occurrence in ingrown hairs on my face.  I think my skin was adjusting to the new, closer shave though, because after that first week I haven&#x27;t had any complications with my skin.  The shave is remarkably smooth, however, and I think it holds up well compared to a standard disposable razor.  The only limitation is the giant shaver head size.  If you have neat facial hair it is difficult to trim around it while manipulating the blades due to the oversized head.  As a result, I now shave most of my face with the Panasonic and then take 30 seconds to trim up the sides of my goatee with my old Cruzer.  If you have complex facial hair you&#x27;ll probably need to develop a similar method to maintain straight lines of a beard or &#x60;stache.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Overall, the ES-LA63-S provides a surprisingly good, close shave.  I knock it down to four stars because it&#x27;s not great for maintaining facial hair patterns, and at $300, you probably want your shaver to brush your teeth for you as well.  If you don&#x27;t have facial hair and you can swallow the $300 price tag, you&#x27;ll be hard pressed to find a better electric shaver.close for an efficient shave.     <li> The Panasonic ES-LA63 is fairly unusual for a high end electric shaver: unlike its competitors, it does not come bundled with fancy ultrasonic cleaning and charging stations, does not have a built-in lotion dispenser... The box just contains the shaver itself, a world-compatible charger, and a soft case.    The shaver itself does not have all sorts of complicated settings, either: just an on/off button and a three position switch (floating head, locked head, trimmer). Its only concession to the high end is a nifty blue LCD display that shows the amount of time in use and a remaining time estimate. The power button can also be locked by a slider to prevent unwanted activation when traveling.    The trimmer is a bit of a disappointment: it&#x27;s hidden by the large shaving head, so you can&#x27;t really see what you&#x27;re doing with it, rendering it useless unless you&#x27;re doing large areas.. unfortunately it&#x27;s too narrow to be really useful for that type of job. Bottom line, if you need a trimmer, buy a $20 Wahl at Target: this one won&#x27;t... er... cut it.    The large shaving head is also a problem if you need any sort of accuracy, because it&#x27;s always hiding what you&#x27;re doing.  All these minor problems are eclipsed by the amazing quality of the shave: as close a shave as you would get from a mechanical razor, and absolutely none of the redness or pain you would get from an electric shaver. I have never seen this type of results from an electric shaver before.    Cleaning is a breeze: pop the head cover, rinse the head and cover under the tap and air dry.    CONS  ----  * Large, can be cumbersome and lacks accuracy (not very good for trimming facial hair)  * Useless trimmer  * Expensive    PROS  ----  * World compatible charger  * Floating head effortlessly follows face contour  * Amazingly efficient and close shave without pressure, pain, redness or irritation  * Easy cleaning    CONCLUSION  ----------  The ES-LA63 is a no-frills shaver, but it puts the emphasis where it really counts: a close, comfortable and painless shave, the best I&#x27;ve ever had by a long shot. I&#x27;d much rather have that than a gimmicky self-cleaning stand, especially when cleaning is such a quick and easy procedure. Very highly recommended.</li>

    <li> I&#x27;ve experimented with electric razors for years. I have a pretty thick beard, and sensitive skin, and trying to find a lasting, close shave for over 20 years has been next to impossible. Shaving against the grain with a standard x-amount of blades razor is too painful, and usually precludes shaving for a day or two until the irritation goes away. I even tried a straight razor shave at Art of the Shave, and horrified the poor woman who painstakingly tried her best to reduce the mess/discomfort. Electric razors throughout the years would burn, and were awful in removing hair from my neck. In the past few years I&#x27;ve tried newer razors from Norelco and Braun, with the same basic results - and got tired of funky cleaning systems and having to buy special solutions for the razors. Being a sucker for yet another electric do-dad, I had to jump on the opportunity when this appeared as a Vine Voice option.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;After 5 weeks of using this razor, it has become my everyday razor for several reasons, which I hope to get across below.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;The first thing that grabbed my attention is that it&#x27;s a no-nonsense razor. The box includes the razor, a nice travel pouch, a cord and instructions - no funky charging/cleaning base, no cleaning cartridges or other solutions. Cleaning instructions are to use water and liquid soap, so just about any modern day bathroom (public or private) is equipped to clean this razor.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Next was the ability to use it with water and shaving cream - just like a standard, x-bladed cartridge razor. It isn&#x27;t until the first time you really try this when you realize that is really modern shaving - comfortable, quick and effective. The razor glides over your skin smoothly, unlike the older dry shave days of electrics (I realize there have been razors that have done this for a while - this was my first time trying it), no burn, no cuts or nicks as with cartridge razors. When you seem to be losing effectiveness, a quick dip of the shaver head in running water cleans the blades and starts fresh - again, just like \\&quot;normal\\&quot; shaving. I had no problems with changing the angles I used to shave in order to get most (but still not some problem areas) on my neck and jawline (which are quickly cleaned up with a cartridge razor). Then a quick clean with the soap and water, final rinse and drying, and in about the same time I&#x27;d take for a normal shave, I had an easier, and closer shave with no burn, nicks or other irritation.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I thought it was just the first day, and expected the typical electric razor problems to crop up over the next week.     <li> The first thing I should say is that you can get as close as you want. Closer than a blade, because with a blade if you add pressure, you get nicks and cutes.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Do you want to get so close that your skin will feel extremely raw? Do you want to get even further beyond where you start bleeding? Even further beyond, I&#x27;ve gotten so close that I&#x27;ve taken out my epidermis, my skin is raw to the bone and I have no hair, smoother than a babies behind; their legs.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;How quick is the shave? Very fast, very quick, very impressive. The head is huge, so that means you can cover a lot of ground in a short amount of time.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Do you want a comfortable shave? Dang, this thing is very very comfortable.  It felt like I was rubbing my face with a cloud. Yes, the blades spin that fast that it feels like you&#x27;ve got some kind of cloudy heat pad on your face. Rubbing it up and down, no irritations, very comfortable. Now if you shave for a while, it will get hot. And, if you shave for a while, your skin will get raw and a little irritated. All depending on how close you want to get. Basically, you won&#x27;t get any irritations if you shave quick; for those with sensitive skin, do not shave for a long period of time. This shaver is very good for sensitive skin.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Does it clean? Yes, put liquid soap on the top, run for a few seconds, and run it under the water. The shaver comes with instructions on how to properly clean. I will also take the top off and rinse off the blades; accidentally hit the blades to the sink while they were on; ouch. It still works though. Then soak the top in alcohol if you want, or set to dry.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;The neck? \\&quot;Conquered the skies, conquered Mount Everest, conquered the moon, CONQUERED the neck,\\&quot; (Phillips commercial) But, the Panasonic es-la63-s also conquers the neck. I had to pull back some of my skin and shave in 100 different directions, but I finally got all of the neck and the only hair remaining is the Adam&#x27;s apple which is too sensitive to shave to the bone.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;It has an LCD screen that tells you how long you have been shaving. And, don&#x27;t worry about dropping it because it has an incredible grip.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Last comments, don&#x27;t shave in the shower, you can if you want, but my experience was that the water slowed down the blades and couldn&#x27;t get a good shave. One important thing: I have very sensitive skin, with a medium to tough beard, growing in a pelthera of directions (a combination that usually spells red, irritated skin). My first Panasonic Razor did so well in addressing this issue that I then ordered this razor (14,000 vibrations vs. 13,000 vibrations of the older model). What an amazingly smooth and comfortable shave (and I shave dry, not wet). I was simply amazed how much closer it shaved. In fact, I kept rubbing my hand over the smooth texture of my skin -- the results were just that pleasant.    Let&#x27;s face it: There is no electric shaver that shaves as close as a razor in one simple pass. After the first pass (with only slight pressure)I then feel which direction my bread grows in the particular area being addressed. I place a little more pressure on the next pass while going against the growth pattern, and repeat the proceedure (if needed) with just slightly more pressure. The biggest mistake any first-time-user makes is pressing so hard on the first pass because they want it to be the only pass. This will never work. An electric shaver is designed to give a very comfortable shave, and the above procedure does just that. I will never go back to a razor (unless, unexpectedly, the power goes out or the water supply is interrupted by some disaster), it is just that comfortable of a shave. GOT A GREAT BUY ON THE RAZOR SO COST DOES NOT EFFECT THIS REVIEW. BEST RAZOR I HAVE EVER OWNED.</li>
    <li> My first foil shaver.  (i&#x27;ve used a couple of rotary Philips shavers in the past.)&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I&#x27;ve had it a couple of weeks, and so far, I like it a lot.     <li> Takes 20+ minutes to shave. Leaves too many unshaved clumps. Cuts skin. Pulls hair. Returning ASAP</li>
    <li> I just purchased the ES-LA63-S to take advantage of the $30 rebate available from Panasonic until 12/31/2010. I upgraded from an older Panasonic model, the very capable ES-8075-S with Vortex cleaning system. The ES-LA63-S model is superior to my older Panasonic, without question. The blades seem a touch more powerful, the shave a bit closer. In addition, the slight curve present in the \\&quot;Arc\\&quot; foil and cutting blades do seem to provide an advantage compared to the \\&quot;straight\\&quot; foil and blades of my older shaver. Note that the ES-LA63-S is the exact same shaver as the more expensive ES-LA93-K; the only difference between them is that the ES-LA93-K comes in black and includes a drying/cleaning/charging base station. The truth is, you don&#x27;t need this station, because the shaver is ridiculously easy to clean under running warm tap water with a little liquid or bar soap, and to air dry. The shaver features a sideburn trimmer, which works fairly well, and comes with a charging cord and black travel case.    This shaver features two motors (one with horizontal oscillation; the other with vertical oscillation), a 14,000 RPM cutting speed, four foils and is made in Japan (some of Panasonic&#x27;s lower-end models are made in China). The blue-backlit LCD screen tells you how much charge is remaining, how much time you&#x27;ve been shaving for, and when the shaver needs to be cleaned. One full charge provides about 40-45 minutes of shaving time. As with all electric shavers, I find some slight touch-up with a razor is necessary afterwards (usually on a small part of the neck), but the bottom line is that by using an electric for the bulk of the shaving, you are saving a ton of friction and irritation on your face.    My personal tips to get the most out of this model:    1) Use a shaving oil (olive oil works great) and warm water and shaving cream for the most comfortable shave. The oil helps provide extra lubrication for the cutting blades as they pass across your skin. I do believe that the use of oil and a wet shave provides for a far superior and more comfortable experience than a dry shave. This is the main advantage of the Panasonic line-up over the Braun series -- the Braun models can&#x27;t be used in the shower or with water and shaving cream.  2) Lock the shaving head so that it doesn&#x27;t move. I find this makes it easier to control the shaver and aim it at specific spots on one&#x27;s face.  3) Clean your shaver after every shave to keep it smelling fresh and clean. This takes 45 seconds at most. Remove the foil top from the shaver and rub liquid hand soap or bar soap lather over the foil and cutting blades. Wash them clean under running warm water. Place the shaver (with foil top still removed) upside down on a paper towel or some toilet paper to \\&quot;gravity\\&quot; air-dry. That&#x27;s it.  4) Drain the battery fully before re-charging it -- this helps to prolong the life of the rechargeable battery.    In closing, bear in mind that Panasonic&#x27;s own literature states that anyone switching to electric shaving from a razor will take about 30 days to fully adjust to it.</li>
    <li> I have used Braun electrics for years. All eventually needed replacement because their batteries needed replacement. They are OK but loud, and take a long time to get a close shave.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;The Panasonic is a little bulky looking at first, but it&#x27;s a good shape and size for the job. The shave is fast and efficient and close. A feature I especially appreciate is the display that measures remaining battery life.  It&#x27;s smartly done: they figure you&#x27;ll get about 10 shaves from a charge (100%), and each reading is a multiple, like 60% remaining. Depending how sleepy I am, some shaves take longer, but you always kind of know where you stand.  I also think that there&#x27;s some reserve power at 0% so you won&#x27;t end up half-shaven. This simple feature ensures that the battery is charged correctly (before it is completely empty) which should allow the battery to last much longer. Also, you know where you stand so don&#x27;t need to bring a cord on trips unless you&#x27;re away for a while.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;The blades oscillate super-fast, and it&#x27;s he sound is a quiet, high-pitched buzz. Much quieter than my old Braun.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Works wet or dry.  I use dry.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Recharge is quick: about an hour.  Then unplug and your good for a week or so.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Cleaning is great.  There&#x27;s a &amp;#34;turbo mode&amp;#34; -- put some soap on the foil, turn on the cleaning mode and run under water, and it basically shakes all the skuzz off, and turns off when done, about 15 or 30 seconds.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Highly recommended.</li>

    <li> The electric shaver vs razor battle has been back and forth for me since I was 16.  I have owned several electric shavers to include a Norelco rotary blade electric razor, Panasonic foil blade shaver, and most recently the Braun 8595 razor.  These shavers would work well for a while, but I just would not get the close shave I wanted, and I would end up going back to the conventional way of shaving while spending hundreds of dollars on disposable blades.  The Braun shaver was probably the best out of all the Electric shavers I owned to this point, but the fact that I had to buy the cleaning solution for it frequently became tiresome.  It is frustrating because I have sensitive skin, and electric shavers give me no irritation,and I do not get razor burn when I use them.  In the profession I am in I am required to look professional, so shaving is scrutinized closely.  In order to get the close shave I need, I have had to use a combination of my Braun shaver and Mach 5 razors because I do not get the shave I need from an electric shaver alone. I have to spend a decent amount of money on expensive shaving creams and after shave balms to help with that close, irritation and razor burn shave. The electric shavers work well in my face area, but always fail in my neck.  I have used electric shavers to shave my face, but use Mach 5 razors to shave my neck.  Because of my sensitive skin, my neck is always irritated after I shave.  With this said I finally broke down and became willing try the latest technology in electric shavers because the cost and time put into shaving were becoming a burden.  Armed with the desire to have a close, quick, inexpensive, and irritation/razor burn free shave, I began looking at reviews from various sites including amazon on the latest electric shavers.  The most important factor I wanted in a new shaver is its ability to give me a close irritation free shave on my neck as this has been my problem area for years. I looked at all brands to include Braun, Phillips, Panasonic, and Remington.  Because I currently owner a Braun Shaver, and based on the positive reviews of the Series 7-760cc, I began leaning heavily to purchasing that shaver.  It wasn&#x27;t until I read and article on line about Panasonic&#x27;s Arc series shavers about how it was designed to shave problem areas such as the neck and chin that I began looking into the Panasonics more closely.  The more reviews I read on the various Arc series shavers, the more I began to see that these razor may be what I have been looking for all these years.  I ruled out the Braun based on the price and having to deal with the cleaning solution again.  I narrow the search down to two shavers, the Panasonic ES8243A Arc IV and the ES-LA-63 Arc IV.  Both have overwhelming reviews and both are rated and 4 1/2 stars.  The LA-63 is about $50 more, but still considerably less expensive than the Braun.  Based on what users have said in their reviews, I felt the LA-63 would suit my needs in shaving.  I bought the LA-63 two weeks ago.  In its first task, I had not shaven in a week and had a considerable amount of facial hair.  The Braun I had had issues with snagging my hair when it got too long.  The LA-63 had no such issue and shaved very smoothly, plus I used it in the shower where as my Braun could not be used wet.  The shaver shaved very quickly too, taking only 3 and 1/2 minutes.  Under my old shaving routine, it would have taken about ten.  I was amazed at how smooth my face was after I was done shaving.  The best part is that I had little irritation and no razor burn.  I did experience some irritation, but this was expected as there is a period of adjustment whenever a new electric razor is used.  The shaver also cleans easy because you can use hand soap and do not have to rely cleaning cartridges.  The 5 minute quick charge is also a nice feature.  Though there were many positive features, the shaver let me down in one area, the neck.  The shaver could not clean up all of my neck and left several patches of hair.  I tried going over these areas several times, but only caused my self irritation.  I had to used a conventional razor to shave my neck area.  This was a big disappointment because one of the reasons I bought the razor was the Arc series shaver was designed to tackle the neck hair.  I did not want to give up on the razor yet.  I figured I would give it some time and try shaving wet and dry, and use different types of shave creams.  The results were that I still got a close, smooth shave on my face, but the neck still was a problem area.  Shaving dry did help get a little close with the neck, but it still was not perfect.  It was about to give up on this razor when I discovered Aramis Lab Series Electric Shave Solution.  Using this product in combination with the LA-63 gave me that close shave on my neck I need without razor burn or irritation.  I now have no complaints about this razor and it is the best electric shaver I have ever used.</li>

What I got was a hair pulling torture device.  If you went more then 1 day without shaving, it would punish you by randomly pulling hairs out while shaving.  I tried new blades, same problem.  I barely used this razor.  Purchased in 2010:  Panasonic ES-LA63  Pros:  - GREAT shave, closest shave on a electric, bar none  - DOES NOT PULL STUBBLE!!! (I cannot say this enough)  - Wet/Dry is nice, especially for cleaning  - Lots of shaving surface, shaves quickly  - Good blade life (got a year from the last set)  Cons:  - Cannot run while plugged in, this is inconvenient if you need a quick shave and the battery is dead  - Like all electrics shavers I have used, it struggles when stubble is long (2+ days) and on stubborn neck hair  - Blue LED is bright (i.e. flashes when charged) which is annoying at night  - Expensive!  Overall, this is the best electric razor that I have ever used.  I had originally thought the list price was a bit much, however I must admit that I would pay the list price ($120 right now).  If you have sworn of electrics, I would suggest you give this razor a try.</li>

    <li> I regularly use a blade razor for the majority of my shave and then use an electric shaver to clean up the nooks, crannies, and tender spots. I mention this to let you know that I&#x27;ve been using an electric for years so I have a good basis for comparison. The 2 critical features of an electric shaver to evaluate, in my opinion, are closeness of the shave and ease of use. The closeness of the shave for this razor is fine, it&#x27;s as good or better than my current shavers, which are a Panasonic and a Braun (one for home and one for travel). Unfortunately, it&#x27;s not as close as a blade shave. I&#x27;ve yet to find an electric shaver that shaves as close as a blade and after testing this shaver, I&#x27;m still looking. I will say that it is very comfortable to shave with however. It&#x27;s quiet and smooth, no pulling of the whiskers.  We&#x27;ll see what happens when the blades get dull but until then it&#x27;s completely painless to use. This applies to both the wet shaving and the dry shaving. I found no appreciable difference in the closeness of the shave between wet and dry. The ease of use is above average. The handle is comfortable and fits well in your hand. The lcd display is easy to read and has some good info and some useless info. It will tell you how much of a charge you have left and when it&#x27;s time to recharge (useful). It holds a charge for quite awhile. I&#x27;ve been using it for about 3 weeks now and it&#x27;s still operating on the charge it came with. It will also tell you how much time used on the current shave (useless). The blade head of this shaver is huge. It&#x27;s about the size of a tangerine which makes it pretty useful for the big areas of your face but pretty unwieldy for the areas like under your nose and around your sideburns. There is a pop-up trimmer for sideburns that works well, although I have a tough time getting it to line up straight. Overall it&#x27;s a pretty good shaver but loses points for the size of the blade head and for the very high price. I can&#x27;t imagine why anyone would want to pay that much for an electric razor. I wouldn&#x27;t recommend this unless it was about $200 cheaper.ld want to pay that much for an electric razor. I wouldn&#x27;t recommend this unless it was about $200 cheaper.</li>
    <li> Electric shavers  ----------------  If you buying an electric shaver for the first time, skip this section and read the next    Electric shavers basically come in 2 types - Rotary (philips norelco) &amp; foil (braun &amp; panasonic)    Rotaries are good for cutting longer hairs let us say you skip to shave over a holiday then start shaving on Monday morning. Foil shavers are faster and easier to adapt to, since they are very much like your gilette razors, but there are a few downsides - foils are difficult to clean since the hair gets trapped in the inner chamber and foil shavers give you more burn compared to rotary blades.     This is a foil shaver    About Panasonic ES-LA63-S  -------------------------  First of all, I am apalled by lack of product description by Amazon/Panasonic for this product on this product page (atleast as of Nov&#x27;2009).  There is a very informative comparision chart between all the Panasonic foil shavers on this page:     I would suggest that a buyer needs to browse though this product comparison list before jumping into a buy decision:  http://www.amazon.com/Panasonic-ES8109S-Vortex-Technology-HydraClean/dp/B000VKZMHK/ref&#x3D;sr_1_6?ie&#x3D;UTF8&amp;s&#x3D;hpc&amp;qid&#x3D;1257820434&amp;sr&#x3D;1-6    Shave Quality  :  Rotary shavers have never been able to offer me the kind of close shave that I have been able to get through this particular foil shaver.   I have tried cheaper foil shavers before, but almost always it has left me with razor burns.    East of use  : The flexible heads make it very easy to shave around the neck.  If you are graduating from a Gilette to this one - you will find that this is much easier to adapt to than a rotary shaver.  Someone even after 3 years of being with rotary shavers, I still get a bit fearful as I take my rotary shaver around the neck, but not with this Panasonic foil shavers    Hygiene &amp; Safety  :  Why is hygene all the more important in an electric shaver ?  You see the blades are so much close to your skin and obviously they do scrape offlive matter into an enclosed chamber along with the hair.  Now, if you these blades were not to be hypoallergic, they would encourage growth of these live matter along with bacteria.  But the Panasonic ES-LA63-S comes with hypoallergic blades which ward off growth of such bacteria and keep it clean, of course you have to do your due diligence of rinsing the blades in hot water and cleaning it.    Panasonic should have bundled the hydraclean system along with this shaver instead of creating a new model ES-LA93-K priced at $100 more than this.    Other features  : Not too worried about the other features such as battery life - it is not a mobile phone to be held in hand for hours together - almost ALL the shavers in the market today offer a charge to last for a couple of days, which is good enough.     -- Another important thing is to dual voltage operability if you travel to Asia/Europe and this shaver can work with dual voltages  -- 14000 rpm : the faster the foil vibrates, the more efficient it is in giving a clean shave on the very first run and this is currently the fastest in the market    Comparison to Braun  : Sorry, I do not have a clue as to how Braun shavers are - they make foil shavers too.  Remington and Philips make rotary shavers.   But I did do some research on foil replacements and found that Panasonic foils are less expensive compared to Braun foils - obviously Panasonic shavers will cost a lot less to maintain over the years      Value for Money  : An investment in a good electric shaver really pays over time - no price is small to wake up each day in the morning, get a clean shave in a minute or two and walk out confidently.  Not with a $20 shaver or even the most expensive rotary shaver will you get this kind of a feeling - I can tell you from my own personal experience.   I did not realize this until I started using the a quality foil shaver like this.</li>
    <li> The Panasonic ES-LA63-S gives an incredible shave, no doubt about it.  It&#x27;s not often I give 5-star reviews, but this razor earns it despite the price.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;After opening the package, charging for a measly 1 hour, it was ready to go, and I took it into the shower with me that night.  I shave in the shower so this is nothing new, and I had been doing so with a \\&quot;lesser\\&quot; Panasonic wet/dry shaver, the ES8249K Arc IV Nano Vortex, which includes the cleaning system.  Worrisome when receiving this considerably more expensive shaver was that it did NOT include the cleaning base into which the razor is inserted.  But, for that night, I didn&#x27;t think about it.  I lathered up with shaving cream, switched on, and received, simply, the best shave I have ever gotten.  That&#x27;s no hyperbole - this razor managed to out-shave the razor I previously thought gave the best-ever shave, relegating my Arc IV to counter-queen status for a while.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I followed instructions and shaved for several weeks with the new razor alone, then tried the Arc IV again just to make sure.  What I noticed was surprising.  It&#x27;s not *after* the shave that the difference is so shocking.  It&#x27;s the shave itself that is surprising.  The ES-LA63-S shaves smoother and easier than the Arc IV, but the resulting shave is similarly close.  My wife can&#x27;t tell the difference, in fact.  But the during-shave experience is sharply different, and for those who have \\&quot;difficult beards\\&quot; or sensitive skin, I think this is the razor for you.  I have noticed, as one who suffers from, since switching over, less irritated skin and less missed hairs.  It manages to shave extremely close without burning at all.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;On the flip side, there&#x27;s the price.  This razor is considerably more expensive than even my Arc IV with cleaning system, which isn&#x27;t cheap.  But I wouldn&#x27;t complain about that - it&#x27;s a fantastic razor that also includes a great self-cleaning system.  However, with that cleaning system comes the repetive cost of cleaning filters.  If they do the job, and they do, I won&#x27;t complain.  But the razors themselves are equipped with Turbo mode created just to clean it of anything that dirties it, so this cleaning system does seem a little unnecessary.  Just pour some liquid soap on the head, hold the power button for a couple of seconds, and it will jump into Turbo mode for about 20 seconds.  Remove the foil/head cover, add more soap, put it in Turbo again, and you&#x27;re done.  With the Arc IV&#x27;s cleaning system, it would go through a 2-hour cleaning cycle and I&#x27;m not really sure what is going on that takes so long.  Is Turbo mode harder on the razor than the cleaner would be?  Only Panasonic knows, and time will likely tell us who lack the cleaning unit the answer.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;One minor quible: I simply do not understand why the digital readout is not visible while the razor is being used.  The Arc IV&#x27;s display remains lit while it&#x27;s on, displaying both the time the razor has been in use as well as the battery power remaining.  The ES-LA63-S&#x27; display goes blank, only to re-light once it has been turned off.  I simply don&#x27;t understand the point of that.  If it&#x27;s to preserve battery life, it seems a minimal trade-off.  I&#x27;d prefer to have the information available while I&#x27;m using it.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Speaking of battery life, in just over 3 weeks of pretty much every other day use for approximately 4 minutes each time, it has been recharged just once, and it required one Turbo-mode cleaning in that time as well.  If you&#x27;re looking for a low-maintenance wet-dry shaver and don&#x27;t mind the high cost of admission, I don&#x27;t think you can go wrong with this razor.s.     <li> Prior to purchasing the Panasonic ES-LA63-S, I used Gillette Fusion ProGlide in combination with &amp;#34;Nivea For Men&amp;#34; shaving foam. The Gillette blade delivered a perfect closeness and made my skin feel very soft. However, because my skin is quite sensitive, I sometimes got red spots and cuts on my face when conditions were not optimal. I could mitigate this problem by shaving under warm shower and applying the foam for a longer period beforehand, but this whole procedure took a lot of time.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;A decade ago I had owned an electric shaver from Panasonic, but the results didn&#x27;t come even close to a neatly executed blade shave. At some point I stopped using the electric shaver and relied on the blade only. Thirteen years later, as technology has made a substantial advancement, I reconsidered buying an electric shaver again and I expected it to perform better than my old one.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;So I compared the technical details and reviews of some high-profile models, and the new Panasonic ES-LA63-S not only had very good ratings, but was sold at a price much lower ($150) than originally. So I thought to give it a chance.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;After using it for two months, I can conclude that I made a right decision by buying the new Panasonic shaver. Here are some of my experiences that I want to share with any potential buyers:&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;During the first weeks, shaving dry delivered better results than my old Panasonic shaver, but the difference between Gillette Fusion ProGlide was still significant. The new Panasonic model can be used in a dry and wet mode. I think this is a big plus, because I have found that using the shaver under the shower produces a noticeably closer shave than using it dry, especially when I apply the foam in small quantity. Another reviewer has noticed this as well. After two months of using this shaver on a regular basis, I can attest that the dry method works better than it did initially: The shave is closer and it takes less time to complete it. The manual states that the skin needs about a month to adapt to a new shaver. I was skeptical about this statement when I read it first, but now it seems that there is some truth behind it.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;The question of interest for anyone is: How does the electric shaver fare against Gillette Fusion ProGlide for me personally?&lt;br /&gt;I would say that when used wet with the shaving foam, the Panasonic comes as close as 95% to the blade. I consider this as a very good result. The 5% &amp;#34;deficit&amp;#34; is only going to be noticed after one day, when hair growth can be already noticed after using the electric shaver, whereas petting the skin after using Gillette ProGlide still feels quite soft. However, that advantage comes at the cost of higher risk of irritations and cuts, which so far I have never had with the Panasonic shaver. I gladly accept the lack of irritations over the nuance in difference between closeness. Using the shaver dry produces a result of 85% these days when expressed in above numbers, which is still very good to me considering the time savings. Since I have owned the Panasonic shaver, I have never used the blade for my facial hair any more - only for hard-to-reach body and neck hair. Again, Gillette Fusion ProGlide is still the champion in the closeness category, where the Panasonic shaver is just almost as good when used in wet mode. However, given the lack of problems with skin irritations and the time savings, I would say that the Panasonic shaver has proved to be a better option for me overall.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;The other advantage of the electric shaver is that it retains its closeness over a longer time period than regular blades (which need to be exchanged for new ones more frequently). Even though the electric shaver requires a higher initial investment than a blade shaver, I think that the expenses break even at a point when the electric shaver still performs well. Cleaning the electric shaver is not a problem at all: Just put some liquid soap on the blades, activate the motors and rinse it with water. This will keep the shaver clean and will make it a pleasure to smell. The other model that comes with a cleaning station is not really needed in this regard.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Other reviewers have already criticized the battery life on this razor. I can indeed concur with that because I have found that a full battery charge provides energy for just about five 6-minute sessions (this is how long it takes for me to get a neat shave). This is not a lot, but on the positive side, the time to fully charge up the battery is short, too (just about an hour).&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Here is my comprehensive list of pros and cons:&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;+  Can be used in both dry and wet mode.&lt;br /&gt;++ Closeness almost as good as with Gillette Fusion ProGlide when used wet.&lt;br /&gt;++ No skin irritations and cuts&lt;br /&gt;+  Easy to use and easy to clean&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;-  Short battery life (but it charges fast).&lt;br /&gt;-  When fully charged, the display blinks until the plug is removed, which can be annoying (although not a big deal).&lt;br /&gt;-  The motor is a little noisy, but not nerve-wrecking.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;That&#x27;s it for now. I think this shaver has deserved five stars given the highly appreciated positives and the fair purchase price. Should anything be added to my experience, I will update this review.</li>

You pop the top off, put a few drops of hand soap on the blades and turn it on turbo mode. After a few seconds of it foaming up, you simply rinse it under running water and it is spotless. It runs the same speed all the way down to when it tells you it is time to recharge.    About the only thing that could make this a better razor would be if you could run it with the power cord if the battery ever went dead. It is battery power only.    So if you are looking for the most amazing electric razor ever invented, I think I can safely say, you have just found it. How good is it? I give it TEN stars!!!</li>
    <li> Background:  Been shaving with blades for many years, but the cost of my preferred blades has increased over time to the point I started to look around for alternatives.    Last year I spent roughly 140 on blades.  Looking at the cost of an electric it seems that I would save some money (although not a lot) over a two year period including one replacement head.  Time will tell.    So, on to my thoughts about the LA63-S Arc IV:      The Good:  Shaves much faster than my traditional blades.    Fairly close shave when compared to my memory of using a rotary style shaver 15 years ago.    Battery lasts about 10 days for me, better than I expected.    Like the shave time duration feature - but likely because I love measuring things.    Can shave wet or dry - I seem to get a slightly closer shave when dry - but the wet shave is more comfortable to my skin.      The Weak:  Not as close as a blade.  The LA63 shave lasts about 14 hours, then stubble becomes noticeable.  I suspect this is typical of the electric shaver class - perhaps a bit better.    Head does not glide easily over my face - I have to concentrate to not press too hard or it will burn.        The Ugly:  Nothing really - at least not in the first month of use.      Additional thoughts:  Usage technique may matter a lot - and as I am new to foil shavers I might not be doing it \\&quot;right.\\&quot;  But so far the most effective technique (for me) is to use gentle small circling motions on the difficult area&#x27;s of the face:  under the nose, across the chin and jaw bones and around the adams apple -- rather than long sweeps across the face.  And less pressure is better - press too hard and you not only fail to get as close as you want, you might \\&quot;burn\\&quot; your skin.</li>
    <li> Panasonic shavers are great and good value for money. Doesn&#x27;t shave a couple of hard spots on the neck but they are hard with a razor as well. I would recommend this product for ease of use, very quick to clean, good battery and a good shave.</li>
    <li> I found the three top of the line electric shavers - Braun Series 7, Panasonic es-la63, and Phillips Norelco 3D -  to be so similar as to recommend any of them as excellent shavers, but each has its strengths and weaknesses. Too many reviewers are only comparing the closeness of the shave, but that&#x27;s only one factor of several that may be most important. Here&#x27;s my breakdown:&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Closeness - Let&#x27;s start with the most popular category. If all you care about is how close you can shave, then I rate the wet-shaved Panasonic and Norelco even, BUT ONLY when coupled with a shaving oil/gel combo such as [[ASIN:B005ACNPLO Remington Alphagel Sensitive Shave Gel 5 oz. (Pack of 2)]] (there&#x27;s a cooling menthol version as well). Another way to accomplish the same thing is by using [[ASIN:B0023XF60Q SHAVE SECRET SHAVING OIL- THE BEST SHAVE EVER! 18.75ML]] topped with [[ASIN:B0032ANCUU Edge Shave Gel, Senstive Skin, 7-Ounces Cans (Pack of 6)]]. These provide the closest shave possible, but, of course, it&#x27;s messy, takes a lot of extra time, and can be a general pain. There&#x27;s no advantage in closeness to using non-oil shaving cream by itself.  Going dry-shave, I may give the tiniest of edges to Panasonic over Braun and Norelco, but all three are awfully close  - to each other and in quality of shave.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Speed - If you&#x27;re in a hurry and want to get in and get out with a dry-shave as quickly as possible, the Norelco wins. The Panasonic is next followed by the Braun.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Comfort - I don&#x27;t have sensitive skin, but the Braun wins out (unless going wet-shave with the oil/gel as described above). The Braun has three speeds so you can go slower for sensitive areas and intensive on less-sensitive places. I just leave it set on intensive all the time and have no problem. The Panasonic is next followed by the Norelco third. The wet-shaving Panasonic and Norelco are the most comfortable of all if you want to put up with the oil/gel prep and clean-up time.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Cleaning - Any auto cleaning system is easier than manual cleaning. Just pop in the shaver and press a button. That said, the Braun is the only system with alcohol in its cleaner to sanitize as well as a detergent to clean and oil to lubricate. Norelco&#x27;s apparently has detergent and lubrication. From what I&#x27;ve been able to tell, the Panasonic solution is only a detergent. Manually, the Norelco is easiest to clean and you can duplicate the auto clean by pouring some of its [[ASIN:B002DHVAZW Philips Norelco HQ200 Jet Clean Solution]] in a dish or mug and whirring the shaver in it for 30 seconds after shaving. The Panasonic and Braun can be rinsed off under a faucet. The Panasonic&#x27;s special cleaning speed makes it slightly easier to manually clean than the Braun.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Maneuverability - If you have a moustache, goatee, beard, long sideburns, or whatever this is a very important category. The Braun is king here with the Norelco second and the larger-head Panasonic last.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Noise - You can hardly hear the Norelco at all. The Braun is a little buzzy and the Panasonic loudest although not irritatingly so. Still, a sleeping spouse nearby will appreciate you using the Norelco most.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Travel - The Norelco is last in this category because you&#x27;ll need to bring the charging stand with you. The Norelco soft case does not hold the stand so that&#x27;s a bit of a drawback. The Braun&#x27;s harder case gives it top honors over the Panasonic&#x27;s soft one, but the Panasonic has an on-off lock that the Braun lacks. Perhaps the Braun doesn&#x27;t need it because the case is harder, and also because the Braun is the only shaver that can run while plugged in with a depleted battery. The other two require a 5-minute charge to give you a few minutes shave. A fully-charged shaver gives you about 50 minutes in each.asier than manual cleaning. Just pop in the shaver and press a button. That said, the Braun is the only system with alcohol in its cleaner to sanitize as well as a detergent to clean and oil to lubricate. Norelco&#x27;s apparently has detergent and lubrication. From what I&#x27;ve been able to tell, the Panasonic solution is only a detergent. Manually, the Norelco is easiest to clean and you can duplicate the auto clean by pouring some of its [[ASIN:B002DHVAZW Philips Norelco HQ200 Jet Clean Solution]] in a dish or mug and whirring the shaver in it for 30 seconds after shaving. The Panasonic and Braun can be rinsed off under a faucet. The Panasonic&#x27;s special cleaning speed makes it slightly easier to manually clean than the Braun.    Maneuverability - If you have a moustache, goatee, beard, long sideburns, or whatever this is a very important category. The Braun is king here with the Norelco second and the larger-head Panasonic last.    Noise - You can hardly hear the Norelco at all. The Braun is a little buzzy and the Panasonic loudest although not irritatingly so. Still, a sleeping spouse nearby will appreciate you using the Norelco most.    Travel - The Norelco is last in this category because you&#x27;ll need to bring the charging stand with you. The Norelco soft case does not hold the stand so that&#x27;s a bit of a drawback. The Braun&#x27;s harder case gives it top honors over the Panasonic&#x27;s soft one, but the Panasonic has an on-off lock that the Braun lacks. Perhaps the Braun doesn&#x27;t need it because the case is harder, and also because the Braun is the only shaver that can run while plugged in with a depleted battery. The other two require a 5-minute charge to give you a few minutes shave. A fully-charged shaver gives you about 50 minutes in each.</li>
    <li> This is an excellent razor, however Panasonic&#x27;s customer service is awful.     <li> These are my impressions of the Panasonic shaver after nearly a month of use.  I&#x27;ve previously used Norelco rotary shavers and Gillette Fusion manual razors. The screen shows what percentage you&#x27;ve used, and has icons which tell you if you need to charge it or clean it.  There is a power button on the front, as well as a lock button (so it doesn&#x27;t turn on accidently).  On the back, there is a setting where you can lock the head from moving.  The back also has the pop-up trimmer.  The shaver has a rubber material on the back so it doesn&#x27;t easily slip out of your hands when wet. There is a clear plastic piece that covers the top foil part.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;PERFORMANCE: Performance was excellent and I received the closest shaves I&#x27;ve ever experienced.  On my cheeks, sideburns, upper lip, and chin, the closeness of shave was terrific.  In just a matter of two or three minutes, my face would be baby skin smooth. It goes into a sonic vibration self-cleaning mode.  Then you remove the outer foil and do the sonic vibration again for the inner portion.  I found it to be easy to clean.  I would recommend doing this at least once a week.  I didn&#x27;t clean it for the first two weeks and the foil had a pretty bad odor to it.  Per the manual, you also need to replace the outer foil every year and the inner foil every two years.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;ACCESSORIES:  For a shaver in this high price range, I found the accessories to be severely lacking. Instead, you get a very small soft case that only fits the shaver, and no stand at all.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;There is no doubt that this shaver is an excellent performer and will provide a very close shave.  The only issue is the high price point.     <li> I had seen comparisons between the ES-LA63-S and the Panasonic ES8243A (which I own also) and wasn&#x27;t too sure that I would see a tremendous difference, but decided that since my foil/blades needed to be replaced on the ES8243A, that I would give the newest model a try. The locking feature, brighter LCD screen, and extra 1000RPM are a nice touch, but that doesn&#x27;t justify the upgrade enough for me like the extra movement does.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I have owned the Norelco Advantage, Panasonic ES8109S, Panasonic ES8243A, and now the ES-LA63-S, and never have I gotten such a close, comfortable, non-irritating shave from an electric for my sensitive skin. The rotary Norelco shaver really irritated my neck, and the other two Panasonics were certainly better than the Norelco, but I always had trouble with irritation on my neck since I had to go over the same area multiple times to get all the hairs. The ES-LA63-S puts an end to all of that! It not only hugs the neck and jawline so well, but feels somehow more gentle than its predecessors despite the increase in RPM. Shaving with the other two always took me 6 minutes or more wet or dry, but I can do a more thorough, less irritating job with the ES-LA63-S in around 2 minutes less time! I much prefer wet shaving to dry shaving also, and use Shave Secret oil because it allows me to see what I am doing in case I need to go back over a certain area and provides me with a slick protective barrier as well. I feel like the ES-LA63-S is \\&quot;rolling\\&quot; across my face because of the freedom of movement rather than my having to force the shaver along like it felt with the others.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;So I would HIGHLY recommend this shaver even compared to its very similar looking predecessor - ES8243A - with the same looking \\&quot;4\\&quot; blades.     <li> After just one use, I wasn&#x27;t convinced that this new Panasonic four-blade shaver really outperforms their excellent three-blade models.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;This morning, though -- my second shave -- this shaver went to work like the little robot bodyguard Mr. Zurkon in Ratchet &amp; Clank, mowing down my whiskers the way Mr. Z. mows down bad guys. Braun. Packed the panasonic up for return to Amazon. Sorry about that.    Think about it people: The Panasonic is discounted more than 50% to an actual price point less than equivalent quality Brauns and Norelcos. I admit I fell for the gimmick that I thought I was getting a three hundred dollar shaver at a fraction of the cost. I figured it&#x27;d be an improvement over a very used Braun. It wasn&#x27;t. You get what you pay for.    Granted, there are a lot of skin and beard types, but having used a couple Norelcos, one Remington, 2 Brauns, I know what to expect from a shaver. The switch to Braun 15 years ago was a completely better experience than what I had before. This time the switch to Panasonic was a step in the wrong direction.    It might work well for you, but don&#x27;t sell yourself on the idea you&#x27;re getting a deal.</li>

After five days or 10-12 minutes of total shaving time, the display indicates the battery charge is down to 50%.  These numbers have been constant for the eight weeks I have owned the shaver.  Knowing that LI-ion batteries do not like being fully discharged, I plug in the charger every five days or so.  Not a big deal I suppose and the shaver is fully charged within 30 to 45 minutes.  Note to Panasonic: The handle is somewhat skinny ever for my small hands so you could increase the battery size and still have a handle that fits the hand.     <li> (UPDATE 11/20/13 - To research complaints about battery drain, I went ahead and did a battery drain test AFTER the display on my shaver showed \\&quot;10%\\&quot; of juice left.  It ran for a FULL 35 minutes beyond this point before conking out.  I think what&#x27;s happening is the display drops in 10% increments after each use, giving users the misleading impression that they&#x27;ve got little charge left especially when they hit the \\&quot;50% left\\&quot; mark.  Based on my \\&quot;battery drain\\&quot; test, this is NOT true.  The battery in this shaver is GREAT, holding a charge that lasts well within the 45 minutes touted on a single charge.)&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&#x3D;&#x3D;&#x3D;&#x3D;&#x3D;&#x3D;&#x3D;&#x3D;&#x3D;&#x3D;&#x3D;&#x3D;&#x3D;&#x3D;&#x3D;&#x3D;&#x3D;&#x3D;&#x3D;&#x3D;&#x3D;&#x3D;&#x3D;&#x3D;&#x3D;&lt;br /&gt;ORIGINAL REVIEW BELOW.&lt;br /&gt;&#x3D;&#x3D;&#x3D;&#x3D;&#x3D;&#x3D;&#x3D;&#x3D;&#x3D;&#x3D;&#x3D;&#x3D;&#x3D;&#x3D;&#x3D;&#x3D;&#x3D;&#x3D;&#x3D;&#x3D;&#x3D;&#x3D;&#x3D;&#x3D;&#x3D;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;* Until now, I&#x27;ve always believed electric razors could NEVER come close to beating hand-held blades. But this Panasonic comes very close - so much so that I rarely use a straight blade anymore!&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;* Disclosure:  I do NOT work for Panasonic and I am NOT being compensated in any way for this review.  But this [[ASIN:B002N5MHLU Panasonic ES-LA63-S Arc 4 Mens Electric Shaver]] is pure, unadulterated awesomeness, blowing every competing Norelco and Braun shaver out of the water!&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;* Very few people can afford $300 for this machine.  But when it comes up for sale for under $150, which is often - you should snap it up because it&#x27;s worth EVERY penny - and THEN SOME.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;* Unlike other electric razors, this Panasonic cuts so close without nicking up your skin that you won&#x27;t believe your eyes and you won&#x27;t believe your fingers when you run them over your face after each shave.  Neck hair will take longer to shave - but NOT too much longer compared to other electric razors.  (And I have coarse dark hair which grows quickly.)&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;* A blue LED light clocks each session.  When you turn it off, it tells you how much battery life is left, i.e., 90%, 80%, 70%, 60%, etc.  You&#x27;ll get about 45 minutes of shaving on a single charge - or about 10 days worth of shaving without reaching for the re-charger.  (BTW, the reason this shaver won&#x27;t work with the cord is common sense!  Who wants to be electrocuted in the shower with the cord attached?)&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;* Cleaning is a breeze.  Just press the buttons on the right and left sides of the head - and the foil framework comes off easily.  Turn your shaver on and hold the power button down for at least two seconds.  Your shaver will go into a \\&quot;cleaning mode\\&quot; whereby its blades will vibrate like mad, providing the cleaning equivalent of jumping to light-speed in a \\&quot;Star Wars\\&quot; movie - without rattling like the Millennium Falcon.  Just run tap water over the blades and all hair cuttings will vibrate off into your bathroom sink.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;* I&#x27;ve tried this shaver in both wet and dry modes and its performance is superb.  However, shaving in wet mode with a thin cream such as [[ASIN:B004DU3V2M Kiss My Face Moisture Shave Key Lime Cream]] is supersonic awesome.  (Note, shaving \\&quot;wet\\&quot; makes cleaning easier because you&#x27;ll have less facial oil when you clean the heads after every use.)  Unlike Norelcos with rotary blades which pivot a little, the head on this Panasonic pivots up and down AND side to side, hugging your face in every direction.  It has two (2) motors.  One cuts up and down and the other cuts from side to side.  It&#x27;s great at getting rid of 99 7/8% of my neck hair and the nubs in both corners of my mouth.  (More about that \\&quot;1/8\\&quot; difference later.)&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;* This shaver comes with a travel pouch and a locking switch (to prevent it from going on while traveling) - as well as a blade cover.  It also has a pop-up trimmer for bushy sideburns and mustaches.  The head can even be locked to prevent pivoting while shaving.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;* Now, about replacement blades.  Do the math.  Panasonic still wins.  If you have to change blades every six-months-to-a-year - well, no offense, but you&#x27;ve got a genetic profile of a werewolf.  Most people with \\&quot;standard\\&quot; beards won&#x27;t have toreplace the blades on this machine for WAY MORE than a year, and I have a tough, coarse beard.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;* The money you&#x27;ll spend for two (2) [[ASIN:B001159UMM Panasonic WES9068PC Men&#x27;s Shaver Replacement Inner Blades]] - is TINY compared to the cost of replacement blades for other electric razors.  This Panasonic takes two (2) replacement blades - which doubles to four blades - because two additional blades are built into the outer foils - which hook into the base of the replacement blades.  Note that the outer foil unit - [[ASIN:B002N5MHLA Panasonic WES9165PC Men&#x27;s Shaver Replacement Foil]] - does cost more to replace, but you won&#x27;t replace it often (unless you break or puncture it) - because the two blades built into them are designed to cut thicker hair.  These blades are comparable to what&#x27;s found on a trimmer for sideburns, but the foils protect you from getting nicked or cut.  (And I don&#x27;t know anyone who&#x27;s ever replaced the bigger blades on a trimmer.)  Don&#x27;t get me wrong.  You WILL change the two-bladed foil unit eventually, but in the long run, you WILL still save money compared to what it costs to buy one 18-multi-blade blister pack locked up in plastic cases in stores.  If you want to save even more money, buy the foil and the two blades TOGETHER - which are available in the [[ASIN:B002N5MHL0 Panasonic WES9025PC Men&#x27;s Shaver Replacement Out Foil and Blade Kit for ES-LA63-S]].  Buying this \\&quot;kit\\&quot; should save you around $20 to $30 than buying these items separately.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;* I&#x27;m taking away a \\&quot;half-star\\&quot; (even though fractional-stars aren&#x27;t allowed here) - for one reason.  While this is the BEST electric razor I&#x27;ve ever used - note that in my first paragraph above, I said \\&quot;this Panasonic comes very close\\&quot; to beating a hand-held blade.  After a wet shave (which I recommend over dry if you&#x27;re not in a hurry) - I run my fingers over my cheeks, jaw bone and neck.  They slide like a sled on snow across my face and jaw line - and over 99 7/8% of my neck.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;* But there are always one or two tiny spots on my neck this razor won&#x27;t completely get.  Now, you might ask, \\&quot;well then what&#x27;s the point of buying this [[ASIN:B002N5MHLU Panasonic ES-LA63-S Arc 4 Mens Electric Shaver with Dual Motor and Multi-Flex Pivoting Head]] if it&#x27;s not as good as a blade?\\&quot;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;* This is my response:  Shaving is one of the most aggravating and time consuming chores men face EVERY day.  The type of finish you will get with this [[ASIN:B002N5MHLU Panasonic ES-LA63-S Arc 4 Mens Electric Shaver with Dual Motor and Multi-Flex Pivoting Head]] is EQUAL to using a hand-held blade for, let&#x27;s say, four minutes.  Think about it.  During my hand-held \\&quot;blading\\&quot; days, unless I was headed to a special event - I did NOT spend as much time to get at every cotton-picking nook and cranny on my neck, especially the area below my ears.  I could still FEEL tiny bristles, but I could not SEE them.  When 100% smoothness was required, I spent more time WITH A HAND-HELD BLADE to get at those nooks and crannies anyway.  Hence the \\&quot;touch up\\&quot; conundrum.  Today, I STILL keep a hand-held two-blader nearby if perfection is my goal.  But most of the time, I don&#x27;t bother.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;* One last thing.  Don&#x27;t mess with electric shaving kits which come with \\&quot;immersible tubs\\&quot; filled with expensive cleaning solutions.  Panasonic recommends just liquid soap and water to clean the heads.  (After shaving in wet mode, I don&#x27;t even bother with soap.  The residual suds from the [[ASIN:B004DU3V2M Kiss My Face Moisture Shave Key Lime Cream]] and a strong blast of tap water while the heads are in \\&quot;cleaning mode\\&quot; does the job for me.  If I want to clean after shaving dry, I just use a blast of tap water, no soap.)&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;* Yes, the $300 price tag is steep and yes, you get what you pay for.     <li> This is the third (may be fourth) Panasonic shaver that i have had as I like to shave whilst showering. I use a good quality shaving cream Crabtree and Evelyn - not a foam - which is very cost effective as only a small amount is necessary with a pot lasting up to six months. A foam is not required because the shaving action causes to cream to foam as the shaving progresses.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I have noted some comments on battery life, or perceived lack of it. I would support the statement that there are about five shaves per charge and that the shaver can not be used whilst connected to a power supply. In order to prolong the battery life, I follow recommendations on batteryuniversity.com and charge the battery when it has 50% charge left.&lt;br /&gt;- It is cheaper to shave with electric shaver than with cartridge razor.&lt;br /&gt;If you use this shaver every day for a year and trash it after this, each shave will cost you $0.24 (I got my shaver for 89$). However this shaver will most likely last for more than one year, so cost per shave could be even lower.&lt;br /&gt;DE razor cost per shave &#x3D; $0.02, given that you trash a blade after 5 uses.&lt;br /&gt;G Fusion cost per shave &#x3D; $0.62, given that you trash a cartridge after 5 uses. Gillette&#x27;s promise that one cartridge can last five weeks is laughable unless you shave once a week.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;- The charger is 110 / 240 V, so you do not need to have any additional chargers if you travel abroad.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I have not discovered any significant Cons yet!&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Overall, I am very satisfied with this product.</li>

    <li> Well like the subject states, this was my first electric shaver in 25 years switching after switching from Gillette Powerglide 5 blade razors.  There are hundreds of reviews going over the features so I&#x27;ll just add what I drew from my experience.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;- The most important tip above all tips is to read the manual before you use it.&lt;br /&gt;- When switching shaving methods for any razor, allow 30 days before you judge the shave. When I first started using it it was horrible, took me 8 minutes and I had to go over it several times and  I had patches of stubble and wanted to return it.  After a month, I&#x27;m down to 3-4 minutes and it is almost as close as my 5 blade shaver and I am totally pleased over all.&lt;br /&gt;- The shaver works much better wet if you pre wash and use some shaving lotion, I really liked the Kiss My Face product.&lt;br /&gt;- I also found it worked much better using Williams Electric Pre shave lotion to soften the whiskers before applying shaving cream if I don&#x27;t shave for a few days.&lt;br /&gt;- Use short slow, light, smooth and even strokes and go both directions until you can no longer hear it cutting any whiskers.  You will not get it to shave closer by pressing harder.  Electric shaves will never feel as close as a blade shave because it does not take off a layer of skin (which is healthier)  It does however pull the whisker up and shave under the skin for a better shave if you do it right. I learned the hard way when it stops then has you by the short hairs, it hurts when you pull it off your face, LOL!  So if you are one of those that believes you need to bleed the power dry don&#x27;t do it on your face.  So everything works fine, lots of power, easy to clean, and it just lays on its side on my sink.  Who needs a stand?
