    <li> Update 7/17/17; Update 12/1/12; original review 10/9/10.  Update about 7 years later...  I&#x27;m still using this razor, though I&#x27;ve changed the foil and blades a number of times.   At this point the digital display is dead and the razor head is stained with soap/shaving cream that won&#x27;t come off. But it still works, holds a charge for a long time, and gives a good shave.   * * *  12/1/12  After two years I replaced this razor. Could you get more life out of it than two years? Definitely. Why did I replace it?  1. Mold, despite regular cleaning regime.  * After about 18-20 months, this razor started to get black mold on/in the plastic under the foil cover, on the part of the razor where the blades are attached. This part of the razor is a light color plastic, so it could be easily seen. It does not rub off; it is in the plastic and like a stain. I should add this problem emerged even though I ALWAYS took off the foil cover, rinsed the foil cap and blade area of razor after use, and left the two parts out on the counter to dry. I can only imagine that not doing this cleaning routine (a quick rinse and putting it in a drawer) would leave one with a very moldy razor.  * I tried cleaning the mold with a bleach solution, soap, and hydrogen peroxide. Helped but didn&#x27;t get rid of it. I&#x27;m sure the mold was also within the razor in areas that I couldn&#x27;t see.  * I think this was mostly a cosmetic issue, but I didn&#x27;t like the idea that there would be mold near shaving blades and my face.  * If you have a black version of this razor you probably have the same thing happening, but you don&#x27;t see it. It might be a good idea for everyone to give their wet razors a dunk in hydrogen peroxide or a bleach solution once in a while.  2. I upgraded to a model with a cleaning stand.  * As noted below, I didn&#x27;t really like that this razor didn&#x27;t come with some kind of stand. I knew that I wouldn&#x27;t put a wet thing in a drawer, and if I was going to leave it out on the counter, it felt like it should have a stand.  * Because of the mold issue, I upgraded to a model that would have a stand and the cleaning function. I am hopeful that the cleaning function will eliminate the mold problem with my new Panasonic razor.  * I will write a review of the new razor, but let me just say here that the stand is big, not very elegant, has very bright flashing lights (you won&#x27;t want it near your bedroom at night), and very noisy for about 5-10 minutes (sounds like a train, and in a quiet room feels as loud, no joke-- my wife hates it).  Summary-- Panasonic makes a great razor, but this mold issue was an unexpected disappointment.  10/9/10.  This is an excellent shaver and I&#x27;ve switched happily and probably permanently from blade shaving, only wishing I had switched years ago. But years ago (say 15 to 20) I had used a few different rotary Braun and Norelco electric razors that didn&#x27;t do a great job, and gave them up for blades. This one works differently, whether it is the ultrasonic or the blade style and motion, so if you think you have tried an electric shaver by trying only one kind, I&#x27;ve learned that you have to try all the different types. This one might be the one for you.  I shaved for years with Mach III blades, but even using high quality shaving cream, I came to hate shaving, that knife on my face, which I have to do every day, with a dark beard. This razor give a close shave and it is painless. I continue to shave wet, with no difference than with my blade, and have had no irritation, even with the very first use (so don&#x27;t be put off by that &amp;#34;you have to get used to it&amp;#34; warning). I actually look forward to shaving now, or at least don&#x27;t mind it at all. Granted, I still have my Mach III handy, to clean up a few missed hairs, but I do not mind the &amp;#34;extra step,&amp;#34; since I get a closer shave than I ever have, and without pain and any cuts. (My routine includes Art of Shaving or Body Shop shaving cream, excellent products, a small amount of cream lathered on with a damp shaving brush.)  Shaving is quick with this razor. Its rapid ultrasonic motion creates more lather when you use shaving cream, which makes the shaving even smoother. It takes a few minutes, and you don&#x27;t have to worry about getting cut.  Maybe you can get the same shave with one of the lower priced models, but I am so pleased with it that I don&#x27;t resent the price. I sometimes wish that I had bought a model with a stand however.</li>

    <li> I&#x27;m an electric shaver lover. In fact, you might call me slightly obsessed with the devices (i.e. I have several). I like the Panasonic ES-LA63-S Arc4 for a few solid reasons:&lt;br /&gt;- it&#x27;s light&lt;br /&gt;- it&#x27;s easy to clean&lt;br /&gt;- it has a travel lock&lt;br /&gt;- it provides a smooth, comfortable shave&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;To clean the shaver, simply apply a little liquid hand soap to the head, give a long press on the &amp;#34;On&amp;#34; button to activate the Turbo Clean and run it under hot tap water. When the Turbo switches off (about 20 seconds) remove the head and continue running the tap water onto the head of the shaver and inside the removed head (about 10 more seconds). Then simply shake off the excess water and leave to dry on the counter (I usually put it on top of a face cloth to absorb the water). About once a week I will spray Shaver Saver (either from Remington or Norelco) on the shaver&#x27;s head and run the shaver for about 20 seconds. This lubricates it and helps clean any mineral deposits from the tap water.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;The Panasonic is a linear shaver that runs at 14,000 rpm (the fastest in class). It uses stainless steel blades on a swivel head that can be locked if desired. There are four blades, hence the Arc4 designation. The handle is ergonomic and therefore easily held whether over the sink or in the shower. Yes, you can use this shaver dry OR wet. I do not shave in the shower but on occasion I will shave &amp;#34;wet&amp;#34; over the sink by applying some shaving cream to my face. The resulting shave is extremely close and comfortable.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;The only minor drawback is the size of the head which makes shaving the upper lip a bit cumbersome but certainly not impossible; it just requires a little patience.     <li> I am 47 years of age and been using a blade to shave for my entire life.  However, when considering the cost of a package of 16 Gillette Mach 3 Razors (about $35), I have found myself shaving every other day just to save money on buying refills.  Fortunately my face can tolerate a shave every other day without looking overly scruffy.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;...but I wanted that clean-shaved look day in and day out and figured that perhaps switching over to an electric razor may be a better alternative, saving me money on blade replacements in the long run.  I would have never really considered going electric with the bad reputation such razors have had -- but I do think there have been great strides made in electric razor technology over the past decade.  When I heard about the Panasonic Nanotech shaver in a radio commercial I decided to take a look at the many reviews posted here on Amazon.  I was shocked at how much praise there was for this razor.  I just had to try it out for myself.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I didn&#x27;t rush into this review.  I knew that I had to give my face 3 weeks to adapt from blade to electric.  So, I am giving you an assessment of the Panasonic ES-LA63 now three weeks post purchase where I have shaved just about every day since.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;My initial reaction to using the Panasonic Nanotech shaver is that it&#x27;s extremely comfortable.  Its wide head covers a lot of area and to date I have never felt any pulling of hairs whatsoever.  No doubt, the experience of using an electric over a razor is more preferable as far as comfort and ease.  You never need to press down hard with the electric shaver (in fact you shouldn&#x27;t) and there is never the fear of cutting one&#x27;s self  (though I never regularly cut myself with the Gillette blade).&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I have used the Panasonic both wet and dry.  I suppose I somewhat prefer to use it wet along with KING OF SHAVES ALPHA GEL which is sold here on Amazon and I HIGHLY recommend.  A minute amount of gel goes a long way and really adds comfort to the shave.  The only thing I noticed is that the shave seems to get better 5 minutes in as the skin and gel dries as there is more direct contact with the skin.  In essence, I think the dry shave gets you closer but I do love the initial lubrication that the shaving gel provides.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;No doubt, this electric razor gives you a shave that is as close as a razor.  I run my fingers across my cheek and it feels super smooth as if just shaved with a blade. That being said, the Panasonic doesn&#x27;t do the job nearly as well across the entire area of the face and neck.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Let me go back to the first day of using this razor so you can see how far I have progressed in three weeks....&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;On my first day, I used this razor dry.  I immediately got close, blade results across my face.  However, I found patches of unshaved hair where the face curves right below the ears towards the neck.  And the neck itself was a mess.  I had to repeatedly run the Panasonic across these areas several times, pulling the skin tight in order to achieve the best results.  My neck became red and bumpy from repeated passovers.  Initial total shave time was more than 6 minutes.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Three weeks later I would say the results have improved somewhat.  I have gotten my shave time down to 5.5 minutes.  I am getting more used to the problem areas that need more attention.  I&#x27;m doing a better job getting the side curves of my face below the ear.  However, I still have to put considerable effort into doing several passes to get small patches in the corners of my face..  The neck hasn&#x27;t really improved with the exception that it doesn&#x27;t nearly get as red and bumpy as it used to.  I can get 90% of all the stubble off my neck but there is always small areas that the razor just won&#x27;t cut and that I have to attend to with a dry blade.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Ultimately, the problem with this electric razor is that you&#x27;ll still need to use a quick dry blade to pass over areas of your face and neck to do the job perfectly.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;For instance, I have a goatee.  The Panasonic ES-LA63 does a good job of trimming around the goatee even with its large head.  I just turn it sideways and shave up and down along the goatee line.  However, it doesn&#x27;t do a good job of giving the goatee line definition.  For that I have to follow up with a razor just to define the line.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;The Panasonic features a display which alerts you of remaining charge level and total shaving time.  Unfortunately the display goes off once you start the shave but comes back on as soon as you turn the shaver off.  There is supposedly an indicator letting you know when you need to clean the shaver.  I have yet to reach that point yet.  However, the Panasonic seems very easy to clean.  I always remove the cover and run water through the foil and blades after every shave.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I have been able to get about 6 6-minute shaves before the razor needs recharge.  My immediate concern is how many charges this baby is going to continually allow me before the battery goes sour and it has to be replaced.  I suppose if I get two years out of this Panasonic shaver before that happens I will have gotten my money&#x27;s worth.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;CONCLUSION&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I love this Panasonic razor.  I so much prefer using it over a blade.  Even when it using it with gel and water I find it to be a much more satisfying shaving experience than using blade and water.  Using it dry is even better because you don&#x27;t have to deal with cleaning up the sink full of shaving cream and water.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;That being said, I find it hard to believe that anyone is having completely satisfactory results using an electric razor over a blade.  Yes, the Panasonic does shave as close as a blade across the face.  However, when it comes to the neck and lower sides of the face, you aren&#x27;t going to see perfection.  Even looking at my neck minutes after shaving, I see specks of hair all over the place that the razor just could not cut.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Everyone&#x27;s face is different so I suppose I am part of the unfortunate sect that are going to have difficulty with the neck area.  Perhaps my face still has not completely adapted to the electric razor.  However, judging by some of the reviews I have read I know that the neck area can be a real problem.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Was this a good purchase?  Absolutely.  I love to shave with this thing.  Just have to accept the fact that I have not rid myself of the blade completely.  The Panasonic accomplishes 90% of the task but I still have to do a very quick dry swipe of the blade over certain areas of the neck.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;UPDATE: Now one week later (a full four weeks) I am seeing improved results in the neck area.  Can it be?  Is the Panasonic actually doing a good job on the neck?  It seems so.  I suppose the neck area took a little longer to adapt to an electic razor than the face area.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I am convinced that I will never go back to a blade again.  I love using an electric.  For all of you who are making the switch from blade to motor, just give your face 3 weeks and your neck and additional week to adjust.  It&#x27;s amazing how close this baby shaves.  Just hope this razor lasts at least 2 years.ee.  The Panasonic ES-LA63 does a good job of trimming around the goatee even with its large head.  I just turn it sideways and shave up and down along the goatee line.  However, it doesn&#x27;t do a good job of giving the goatee line definition.  For that I have to follow up with a razor just to define the line.       The Panasonic features a display which alerts you of remaining charge level and total shaving time.  Unfortunately the display goes off once you start the shave but comes back on as soon as you turn the shaver off.   There is supposedly an indicator letting you know when you need to clean the shaver.  I have yet to reach that point yet.  However, the Panasonic seems very easy to clean.  I always remove the cover and run water through the foil and blades after every shave.       I have been able to get about 6 6-minute shaves before the razor needs recharge.   My immediate concern is how many charges this baby is going to continually allow me before the battery goes sour and it has to be replaced.  I suppose if I get two years out of this Panasonic shaver before that happens I will have gotten my money&#x27;s worth.      CONCLUSION    I love this Panasonic razor.  I so much prefer using it over a blade.  Even when it using it with gel and water I find it to be a much more satisfying shaving experience than using blade and water.  Using it dry is even better because you don&#x27;t have to deal with cleaning up the sink full of shaving cream and water.    That being said, I find it hard to believe that anyone is having completely satisfactory results using an electric razor over a blade.   Yes, the Panasonic does shave as close as a blade across the face.  However, when it comes to the neck and lower sides of the face, you aren&#x27;t going to see perfection.  Even looking at my neck minutes after shaving, I see specks of hair all over the place that the razor just could not cut.    Everyone&#x27;s face is different so I suppose I am part of the unfortunate sect that are going to have difficulty with the neck area.   Perhaps my face still has not completely adapted to the electric razor.   However, judging by some of the reviews I have read I know that the neck area can be a real problem.    Was this a good purchase?  Absolutely.   I love to shave with this thing.  Just have to accept the fact that I have not rid myself of the blade completely.  The Panasonic accomplishes 90% of the task but I still have to do a very quick dry swipe of the blade over certain areas of the neck.    UPDATE: Now one week later (a full four weeks) I am seeing improved results in the neck area.  Can it be?  Is the Panasonic actually doing a good job on the neck?  It seems so.  I suppose the neck area took a little longer to adapt to an electic razor than the face area.    I am convinced that I will never go back to a blade again.  I love using an electric.  For all of you who are making the switch from blade to motor, just give your face 3 weeks and your neck and additional week to adjust.  It&#x27;s amazing how close this baby shaves.   Just hope this razor lasts at least 2 years.</li>

    <li> You know, most of us men have to shave every day (unless we are retired, have a beard, or some disease that prevents facial hair), so one might as well have the cadallic on the market (or close).  This shaver is not perfect; there are a few things that slightly bug me:  first, the head is so big, it is difficult to get just under your nose with the shaver (but not impossible); second, it doesn&#x27;t do all that well with a dry shave and I have had a couple of times of mild razor burn (when wet, that is never a problem).    So, you wonder, why did I give it four stars?  First, it really does shave well in the wet mode, almost all of your face, and it even does a good job on my neck area (most shavers I have used fail the neck test).  You can use it wet or dry; I have always used a shaver dry, but I tried this one with water and shaving cream; it worked all right, maybe a tish better than dry shaving (and there is no chance of razor burn) Third, this unit is super easy to clean; you can put some suds on the foil, turn it on to turbo (just keep start button down for 20 seconds or less), and it will clean the unit.  You can pop the head off and also use this cleaning feature.  You can use water while you are cleaning it.  It always comes out sparkling clean (and cleaning doesn&#x27;t take but a few seconds).  Some people moan about you can&#x27;t shave with the shaver plugged in; you must have the shaver unplugged; this is a safety feature because you can shave with this unit in water (like in a shower or wherever), and Panasonic doesn&#x27;t want you to get electrocuted.  But they have a digital readout telling you how much juice is left.  When you get down to around 20%, you just plug it in.  When it gets charged (like under an hour), a green light flashes, telling you it is fully charged.  Hey, it&#x27;s great!  I have used Braun for years, and I even tried a Remington (nice shave but very cheap units), so I graduated up to this unit.  I hope to have this for many years without problems.  So far, great product.  I know this product isn&#x27;t cheap, but at least you are getting quality for your money.  It even feels like a well made unit in your hand.  When you look at the inside (underneath the foil cover), you see metal and quality,  not junk and cheapness.  If any problems develop, I will come back to this review and comment. I have updated and altered my shaver review.  After having it a couple of months, I am not as impressed; it doesn&#x27;t really shave as well as my cheap Remington dry. When you turn it on, you can lock it on so that it won&#x27;t turn off while you&#x27;re shaving if you happen to bump it.  Also, when you&#x27;re traevling, and if like me you may not have brought your charger, lock the power switch in the off position so that your luggage doesn&#x27;t turn it on and discharge it!&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Overall, I think this is a terrific product at a reasonable price.</li>

I think this is a key feature here.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;The shaver is much more usable without the \\&quot;foil frame\\&quot; where the black foil \\&quot;carrier\\&quot; is exposed. This way the shaver is much easier to get closer under the nose and easier to see what you are doing.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Just remove the foil frame then remove the foil carrier from  the frame. The foil is not reversible so note the orientation, the lone hair cutter goes toward the trimmer.  Then snap the carrier (only) back on the shaver.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;But what to do about securing the cap? I made an elastic \\&quot;chin strap\\&quot; to hold the cap on. Using one of those hair bands with a hole (3/16 drill bit BY HAND) where each release tab \\&quot;bulge\\&quot; is. The \\&quot;chin\\&quot; being that area under the pivot.  Just knot the band on the outside of the cover just like you would for a hat strap. Also if you cut the, now unnecessary, corners with a pair of dykes the cap goes on easier.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt; For the longer and stubborn  neck hairs use the trimmer but drag it up your neck (upside down) with the foil facing down. This shaver now is a Five Star!&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I thought the blank display while shaving was an oversight but if it  showed the time I would check it often and slow my shave time.</li>

    <li> History:&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I used electric razors when I first started shaving.  Then I went back-and-forth between wet/blade shaving and electric razors.  Then I tried a couple of the various &#x27;wet shave&#x27; electric razors about 7-10 years ago, my experience was awful (lots of irritation, poor shaves, difficult to clean).  My facial hair is fairly coarse and thick.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;So I was doing the Gillette  5-blade cartridge wet-shave for many years, and that was okay...not great since the cartridges are quite expensive, but the shaves were okay, and didn&#x27;t irritate my skin THAT much, I could get a few shaves out of each cartridge.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Then, about 6 months ago I got intrigued with all this new elitist &amp;#34;old-timey badger hair brush, double-edged safety blade shave&amp;#34; trend that has become quite popular, with people claiming that this old method actually yields the best shaves.  With all of the videos on You Tube showing big, burly guys with the thickest stubble imaginable shaving their face after bragging about their badger hair shave brushes and fancy blade holders, I was all but convinced that I&#x27;d get the best shave that way.  Wrong...I tried many razors, many creams, soaps, gels, methods, etc., and I couldn&#x27;t get a shave that was EVEN as close and comfortable as when I was using the Gillette cartridge razors.  Sure, double-edged blades ARE cheaper, but my face couldn&#x27;t have cared less about that fact...even after 3 weeks of double-edge razor shaving, the irritation never subsided.  Not to mention that shaving took a frickin&#x27; LONG TIME between foaming a soap with the brush, applying the soap with the brush, shaving, and then having to go over areas again because the single safety blade didn&#x27;t seem to shave adequately closeclose at all...&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;My experience with this razor:&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;So, feeling discouraged that I&#x27;d find a comfortable, easy shave at all, I started looking up wet-shave electric razors, and came across this Panasonic ES-LA63-S Arc 4.  I shave wet (with a shave gel) with it, and it gives me the absolute BEST shave I&#x27;ve ever had, and even when I have 2 days of stubble, shaving with it is easy and the gel provides an excellent reduction in friction.  Even with a couple days stubble, I can finish a wet/gel shave in 5 minutes.  The shave is closer than almost any shave I&#x27;ve ever had, and I don&#x27;t notice any irritation/discomfort with this razor; doesn&#x27;t even seem like my face had to &#x27;adjust&#x27; to the razor, which is uncommon when changing shave methods.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Pros:&lt;br /&gt;-Easy, comfortable, and FAST wet (gel) shave&lt;br /&gt;-Comfortable to hold, nice weight&lt;br /&gt;-Easy to disassemble and clean&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Cons:&lt;br /&gt;-Doesn&#x27;t last a million years on a single charge&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Seems like reviews complain about two things with this razor:  The short battery life, and the fact that the razor won&#x27;t operate while the charging cord is plugged in (i.e., if it runs out of battery while shaving, you can&#x27;t plug in the cord and continue shaving).  First, with the short battery life (~50 min), I don&#x27;t have too much of a problem with that.  I can usually finish a shave after 5 minutes of use, so I can typically get at least a week of shaves from the razor.  And plugging the razor in for ~5 minutes yields enough charge to get at least a shave in (from completely dying).  Regarding the fact that the razor won&#x27;t operate with the charging cord plugged in: this is because the razor is designed to operate wet (in the shower/bath)--OF COURSE it shouldn&#x27;t be operated with an electrical cord under wet conditions, so that feature is disabled due to safety.</li>
    <li> I gave it a rating of 2 stars because it grabs individual hairs and yanks them out -- quite painful.     <li> I like shaving variety;  therefore, I will use an electric razor for a while and then a regular razor/shaving cream a while.     <li> Dear Panasonic:  I am returning my Model ES-LA63-S for replacement.  As you see by the accompanying receipt, I purchased this shaver on December 11, 2013.  I purchased it as a birthday gift to myself to replace the Panasonic ES4283A that I purchased on August 31, 2012, which was a replacement for the Panasonic ES8103S I purchased on December 31, 2009 as a replacement for the Panasonic ES8243A purchased on April 15, 2009.  This last was a replacement for the ES8152NC I bought on July 13, 2006.  In fact, I bought three of these, including two for my sons.  My purchase history goes back further, but you get the picture.  Why you may wonder have I acquired so many Panasonic shavers over so short a time.  There are five main reasons: 1) The close shaves they give are unparalleled.  2) I like to shave in the shower, thus all of the models I have bought are wet/dry.  3) The motors have never failed, although one or two of the recent ones have at times wheezed as though out of breath.  4) The blades last for a reasonable time.  5) The displays do not last.  What happens to the displays?  There is an assortment of failures that begin as small quirks such as a missing diode in a number--for example a 5 may display without its top so that it appears as an upside down question mark--to complete failure, which is the case with the one I am returning.  Until this most recent purchase, I convinced myself that I had just been unlucky with the displays.  However the one on this razor began to fail after only two months and like the others the severity of its failure progressed.  The failures were tolerable at first and through the years I had become accustomed to Panasonic&#x27;s kludge digitals, so I overlooked them.  But then one day everything displayed--blade change, wash, charge, and the time readouts went haywire.  Recharging brought new variations on this failure.  And then nothing at all displayed.  So, having invested many hundreds of dollars in Panasonic wet/dry razors, the displays on all of which have failed, I decided to return this very expensive one (I also still have its two predecessors if you would like them).  Thanks,  Terry Gilliam  PS Within a week of returning this razor for repair, I received a new one to replace the old.  6/27/2015 update: Nearly seven months after receiving it, the replacement is still giving the usual great shaves and the display is working perfectly.  I&#x27;ve added a star to my original review.  If it lasts a year, I&#x27;ll add another.  7/5/2016 update:  Well, it didn&#x27;t last a year.  The replacement failed within a month of my June 27 update.  The good news is that Panasonic replaced its replacement shaver with another new one.  The unfortunate news is it failed as well.  Throughout, the issue has been the same.  The display goes haywire in 4-6 months.  When I returned the latest replacement I was given this lesson: &amp;#34;Our warranty covers two years from the date of original purchase or 90 days from the latest replacement date. Your two-year warranty has run out and so has the 90 days.&amp;#34;  What really rubbed me the wrong way was that several weeks after sending in the shaver I had heard nothing from Panasonic, so I had to call them to find out status and to get the aforementioned lecture.  When I asked about repairing my shaver, I was told &amp;#34;It wouldn&#x27;t really be worth it; we recommend buying a new one.&amp;#34;  I will.  But it won&#x27;t be a Panasonic.  It seems the product reliability and the manufacturer&#x27;s 90-day warranty are well matched. I&#x27;ve changed my rating to match my experience with the product and manufacturer.</li>

    <li> Back in the day, Victor Kiam, who owned Remington, used to advertise his microscreen shavers on TV with the slogan \\&quot;Shaves as close as a blade, or your money back!\\&quot;.  Back when I bought one, some twenty years ago, well, lets just say if people really held him to his guarantee, his company would have gone bankrupt very quickly.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Advance forward to the present - since then I&#x27;ve owned a Braun, one of the earlier Panasonic wet/dry&#x27;s (ES762), one of the earlier Braun self-cleaning models (5709), the Panasonic ES-8043 with the 13,000 RPM motor, and now with this model I&#x27;m on my third Panasonic.  The ES-8043 completely blew all of the previous models I&#x27;ve owned straight out of the water.  The motor was the biggest difference - very fast, and it would just keep going, not slowing down until the battery was actually fully discharged - unlike earlier models where it would slow appreciably after the first few minutes of shaving.  The other big difference was the shaving head tilting side to side.  Previous models I&#x27;d owned had fixed heads, or heads that pivotied forward or backwards.  I found the side-to-side pivot on the ES8043 to be much more helpful.  The one downside to the ES-8043 was the narrow pop-out trimmer, much narrower than on earlier models - well fitted for sideburns, but more time consuming for removing longer hairs on the neck.  Still, this shaver did such a good job I found myself rarely needing the trimmer with it.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Now enter the ES-LA63-S.  Panasonic has done themselves one better.  The motor is even slightly faster than the ES8043.  The head now pivots both side to side and forwards and backwards (superb!).  The trimmer is still narrow, and now its a little bit harder to engage (the head needs to be straight so that it can be locked, and the trimmer then can pop-up), but I need it even less than before.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;One thing about this model is that the shaving head is HUGE.  I thought this would hinder me, but it hasn&#x27;t been a problem atall.  Its not difficult to manuever in the tight areas, such as in the area between the upper lip and the nose.  I think the shaving head pivoting in every direction really compensates for the larger size when it comes to the tight areas.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Once again the motor just goes and goes, and does not slow down until the battery is dead - indicated with plenty of warning by the bright blue illuminated display.  I have not had a problem with the battery life - the only thing I can say is that I think the charge indicator on the display is calibrated incorrectly, or intentionally made to error on the side of getting you to recharge the shaver sooner.  I intentionally ran it down until the batter died.  The display shows the charge status in 10% increments.  I noticed that in the 20-100% range, the indicated charge goes down by 10% every 4-5 minutes.  But I was able to run the shaver for 15-20 minutes more once 10% was indicated.  The motor did now slow at all until the very end, when it slowed down over the last 3 or 4 seconds before shutting off completely.  I wonder if other reviewers who have complained about battery life have let it run down all the way, or are just basing their beliefs that the battery doesn&#x27;t last as long as claimed without letting it run down all the way, instead deciding its time to recharge when the indicator says 10%?&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Cleaning it is very easy.  Rub a little soap on the foils, and turn the shaver on in cleaning mode (hold down the power button until the motor shifts to the ultra-fast speed) while running it under warm water from the shower or faucet.  Remove the foils, and run it in cleaning mode again for 20 seconds under the shower or faucet to clean the inner blades.  As of now I&#x27;ve had the shaver 3 weeks, and doing this after every use I&#x27;ve got it spotlessly clean - absolutely no shaving residue on the foils or around the inner blades at all.  This same shaver is available for more money with a cleaning station.  At first I wondered if it was worth the extra money to buy that model, but there is also the ongoing added expense of buying the cleaning solution from Panasonic, and this shaver is pretty easy to clean manually with a pretty minimal effort.  So I would say get whichever version floats your boat, but know you won&#x27;t go wrong with this model&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;As for the actual shave, I&#x27;ve used it both wet with shaving gel, and dry, and it is astoundingly good for an electric.  Every part of my face is shaved closer than before with the ES-8043.  I really can get that \\&quot;as close as a blade\\&quot; shave over most of my face - I&#x27;m not kidding, I cannot tell the difference between what this does to much of my face versus what I get with a Gillette Mach 3 blade - well, except for the difference that my face is not irritated with the Panasonic and with the Gillette it often is.  The traditional trouble spots for me (corners of the jaw, neck) are not quite as good, but they&#x27;re much better than I got even with the ES8043.  Overall, I am very very pleased.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Right now, this \\&quot;4 bladed\\&quot; series of Panasonics are not the latest model.  There&#x27;s an newer, more expensive series with 5 bladed shaving heads.  I haven&#x27;t tried them, and I can&#x27;t imagine they&#x27;re any worse.  But if they&#x27;re really any better than this model, I&#x27;d say Panasonic has pulled off a miracle, because I can&#x27;t really imagine an electric working any better than this.</li>

    <li> I LOVE this razor.  3 disclaimers.&lt;br /&gt;1.) Some people like rotary razors. If that&#x27;s you, ignore this review. I tried the top of the line Norelco and hated it.  This is a foil razor -- I&#x27;ve had lots of Brauns and Panasonics.  This is the best foil razor I have ever had.&lt;br /&gt;2.)  There are thousands of reviews of electric razors and you will find passionate defenses of and eloquent attacks on each.  Obviously faces differ.  Bottom line: find someone who had the kind of razor you used to have (and liked).  Their reviews will probably be most accurate for you.  Mine have been high end Braun and Panasonic.  My old Braun was falling apart -- even with new blades.  This is the replacement.&lt;br /&gt;3.)  Some people like the &amp;#34;auto clean&amp;#34; features -- they raise the price about $90, give you a big stand into which the razor fits, plus you have to buy expensive cartridges or washing fluid.  Most of them don&#x27;t disinfect.  (I think the Braun may)  Some of them smell disgusting -- the Norelco fluid smells like the cheapest nasty body spray you&#x27;ve ever smelled.  The manufacturers obviously have an interest in getting you to buy a renewable -- think printer toner -- rather than just a device.  They claim it has benefits on efficacy.  Interestingly, I&#x27;ve seen no empirical study beyond the ad copy that the auto clean features actually increase the life, efficacy or cleanliness of the razor over just rinsing the blades with warm water and liquid hand soap (not detergent) every week or so.  If you disagree, and want the auto wash feature -- I admit it sounds cool -- this isn&#x27;t the razor for you.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Why do I love it?  It shaves closer with no tugging or pulling.  It has &amp;#34;nano tech blades&amp;#34; which sounds like marketing BS but it is actually similar to the really fancy blades on the Gillette wet razors.  They really are sharper.  I typically to a light shave with an electric and then shave with a Gillette 4 wet razor.  This was so good that -- even used dry -- it wasnearly as close as the wet razor.  Trimmer is small but very good. Bottom line: superb product.  Highly recommended.</li>
